## 1. Behavior and Emotion Resources | Cook Children's

**Source:** https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/

Title: Behavior and Emotion Resources | Cook Children's

URL Source: https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/

Markdown Content:
![Image 1: Language toggle English](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/interface/language_toggle_eng.png)

Growing up in today's world can be hard. Many children and teens experience moments that cause them to feel anxious, depressed or even suicidal. It can be hard to know when to ask for help or where to find support. Below are resources that Cook Children's has identified to assist you and your family.

![Image 2: Smiling person in a patterned sweater holding a large pumpkin, surrounded by falling autumn leaves and a bird](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/home/illustration-sectionhero-thanksgiving-gratitude.jpg)

![Image 3](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/health-resources/mental-health/adhd.svg)

## ADHD

Support a child with ADHD

![Image 4](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/health-resources/mental-health/anxiety.svg)

Managing moments of anxiety

## Substance abuse

Navigating the challenges of substance abuse

## Roadmap for children’s mental health: A guide for parents and caregivers

The _Roadmap for Children’s Mental Health_ is a video series created by [Cook Children's Center for Community Health](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/ "Cook Children's Center for Community Health") to help inform and support caregivers _._

## Need help finding information?

Finding health information you can trust can be confusing and overwhelming. Let us help. A Cook Children's librarian can send you up to date information from reliable sources.

[Ask a Librarian](https://cookchildrens.libwizard.com/f/AskaLibrarian "Ask a Librarian")

## Raising Joy podcast

We encourage you to subscribe to our **Raising Joy podcast**, which aims to encourage hope and resilience among children and teens. Available on the following networks:

[Joy Campaign](https://www.cookchildrens.org/about/promise-report/everything-for-the-child/joy-campaign/ "Joy Campaign")

[Listen on Apple](https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/raising-joy/id1611665146 "Apple podcast")

[Listen on Spotify](https://open.spotify.com/show/6jugpgE9qVbs0xgpFVsxNT "Listen on Spotify")

## Behavioral health services

Our licensed experts provide **psychology and psychiatry services** for families whose children and adolescents, ages 2 to 18, are experiencing behavioral, neurodevelopmental and emotional challenges.

[Behavioral Health department](https://www.cookchildrens.org/services/behavioral-health/ "Behavioral Health")

[Contact us](https://www.cookchildrens.org/services/behavioral-health/contact-us/?postloginurl=inside.asp?mode=patprefs&liteMode=False "Contact us")

## Training and events for health professionals

#### Suicidal Ideation: Cultivating supportive strategies for children and youth

_3 hours (Virtual-Zoom)_

Learning objectives: Describe the current research on suicidality, recognize the signs and symptoms of depression and risk factors for suicidality, define the steps to assess risk of harm and identify appropriate levels of treatment, describe at least 3 interventions for children/adolescents with suicidal ideation and summarize trauma informed strategies to build a culture of support.

[Watch video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Ez2l_OiJbEc "Watch video")[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/healthy-lifestyles/packet_suicidal-ideation-cultivating-supportive-strategies-for-children-and-youth.pdf "Download PDF")[Continuing Education](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/healthy-lifestyles/wellness-workshop-enduring-notice_aug-25-2023-to-aug-24-2026-003.pdf "Continuing Education")

#### Substance Use: Cultivating supportive strategies for children and youth

_3.5 hours (Virtual-Zoom)_

Learning objectives: Identify at least 3 reasons children and youth might use substances, describe at least 3 interventions for children / adolescents experiencing substance use and explore the various perspectives to build a supportive culture for students and families experiencing substance use.

[Watch video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EJO_sH2H-Pk "Watch video")[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/programs/packet_substance-use_cultivating-supportive-strategies-for-children-and-youth_10.27.23.pdf "Download PDF")[Continuing Education](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/programs/wellness-workshop-enduring-notice_oct-27-2023-to-oct-27-2026.pdf "Continuing Education")

#### Autism: A Spectrum of Support

_4 hours_

Learning objectives include: Gaining an understanding of what autism is and who the diagnosis impacts; identify and describe definitions and terminology associated with Autism Spectrum Disorder; gain understanding of Autism Spectrum Disorder diagnostic criteria; identify characteristics associated with Autism Spectrum Disorder; identify presentation of symptoms across settings and to define Neurodiversity and understand the Neuro-affirming lens.

[Watch video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=a2M8FFcX2cE "Watch video")[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/education/autism-a-spectrum-of-support-sm.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Axles of Anxiety: Who, What, Why

_5 hours_

Learning objectives: identifying the different types of anxiety experienced and how it presents in children and teens; identify at least 3 ways media contributes to anxiety; and describe at least 3 coping strategies parents and professionals can use to help reduce anxiety in children and teens. The target audience for this presentation is mental health professionals.

[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/education/axels-of-anxiety-who-what-why.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Building Resiliency Against Adverse Childhood Experiences

_3 hours_

Learning objectives: gaining knowledge about ACES and how it affects people in diverse populations; identify two ways to practice resiliency in everyday life. The target audience for this presentation is mental health professionals.

[Watch video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=z85VYrU4Clg "Building Resiliency Against Adverse Childhood Experiences")[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/education/building-resilience-against-aces.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Commercially Sexually Exploited Youth, Recognizing and Responding: Denton County Strategy

_4 hours (Virtual - Zoom)_

Learning objectives include: identify at least 3 stakeholders involved in the Denton County Protocol for Care Coordination of CSEY victims; gain understanding of the CSE-IT tool and training and how it is used to identify victims and refer for services; recognize signs of complex traumas and appropriate interventions; identify risk factors for male victims of sex trafficking; recognize the impact of victimization on CSEY victims. Target audience: professionals

[Watch video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vDn-9OMTr1g "Watch Video")[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/healthy-lifestyles/packet_csey-recognizing--responding-denton-co-strategy.pdf?v=vDn-9OMTr1g "Download PDF")

#### Commercially Sexually Exploited Youth, Recognizing and Responding: Empowering Youth & Families

_5 hours_

Learning objectives: recognizing how developments in social media are affecting youth; identify ways to support and build resiliency in the LGBTQ+ population; identify the importance of how effective communication between adults and youth help prevent early childhood abuse; and describe ways to identify and respond to youth at risk of sexual exploitation. The target audience for this presentation is mental health professionals.

[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/healthy-lifestyles/packet_csey-recognizing--responding-empowering-youth--families.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Commercially Sexually Exploited Youth, Recognizing and Responding: Texas’ Holistic Strategy

_5 hours_

Learning objectives: being able to identify specific risk behaviors of Commercially Sexually Exploited Youth (CSEY); learners will review the State’s comprehensive holistic public health approach to address CSEY; learners will identify specific stakeholders involved in a multi-disciplinary approach to coordinated care for victims of CSEY in Denton County; learners will describe the specialized role of CSEY Advocates; learners will be identify specific further opportunities for training and engagement as well as reporting mechanisms for suspected CSEY. The target audience for this presentation is mental health professionals.

[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/education/csey-recognizing--responding-tx-holistic-strategy.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Compassion and Empathy: A Response to Bullying

_3.5 hours_

Learning objectives: recognizing the different types of bullying experienced by children and teens; explore the perspectives of schools and community organizations as they work to address bullying; describe at least 3 strategies parents and professionals can use to promote empathy and compassion in youth; and improve services for children and families through collaboration and resource sharing amongst professionals, families, and the community. The target audience for this presentation is mental health professionals.

[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/education/compassion-and-empathy-a-response-to-bullying.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Encapsulated: The link between substance use disorders & mental health

_3 hours( Virtual-Zoom)_

Learning objectives include: recognize at least 3 ways a co-occurrence of mental health illness and a substance use disorder can impact the type of interventions provided to children and families; and describe at least 3 strategies parents & professionals can use to help children who have parents with a substance use disorder. Target audience: professionals

[Watch video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hE2yG9ORB9s "Watch video")[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/healthy-lifestyles/packet_encapsulated-link-btw-substance-use-disorders--mental-health.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Flipping Our Lens on Youth Challenges: Real Problems, Real Solutions

_3.5 hours_

Learning objectives: exploring the intersectionality of technology and pop culture influences on depression, self-harm, and suicide in youth; describe the effects of technology and social media on children and teens' brain, social, and emotional development based on current research; discuss the stressors and challenges today's youth experience from the perspectives of local teens; and describe three strategies to develop positive coping skills to build social and emotional capacity in youth. The target audience for this presentation is mental health professionals.

[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/education/flipping-our-lens-on-youth-challenges.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Recovery after the Chaos: Empowering the Community to Take Back What COVID Stole

_3 hours_

Learning objectives: recognizing how the power of relationship building can help families with traumatic experiences; describe at least 3 strategies parents and professionals can use to improve self-regulation and promote resiliency; recognize the impact of COVID-19 within the family system. The target audience for this presentation is mental health professionals.

[Watch video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lKGxwSMsjwE "Watch video")[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/education/recovery-after-chaos.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Responding to COVID-19 as a Community

_3 hours_

Learning objectives include: explain the benefits, pitfalls, and dangers of the increased utilization of the internet; describe at least three coping skills community members can use to respond to the stresses of COVID-19; and describe how mindfulness can be utilized practically to reduce stress. Target audience: professionals

[Watch video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PZYE0b5FxTg "Watch video")[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/education/responding-to-covid-19-as-a-community.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Together for Youth Mental Health & Wellness in Denton County, Part I

_4 hours_

Learning objectives: summarizing the value of collaboration when addressing children’s mental health needs as a community; identify behavioral health needs at Juvenile Probation and programs available to Denton County youth; explain at least two wellness strategies mental health providers can employ to practice self-care. The target audience for this presentation is mental health professionals.

[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/education/together-for-youth-mh-pt1.pdf "Download PDF")

#### Together for Youth Mental Health & Wellness in Denton County, Part II

_3 hours_

Learning objectives: identifying what is meant when the term neurodivergence is used; describe how to use de-escalation tools with neurodivergent populations; recognize the connection between mental health and physical health. The target audience for this presentation is mental health professionals.

[Download PDF](https://www.cookchildrenscommunity.org/siteassets/documents/education/together-for-youth-mh-pt2.pdf "Download PDF")

# Anxiety Resources

[![Image 11: Raising Joy Podcast](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/health-resources/mental-health/promo-raisingjoy2.png)](https://www.cookchildrens.org/Recycle-Bin/raising-joy/ "Raising Joy podcast")

![Image 12: Language toggle English](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/interface/language_toggle_eng.png)

Cook Children's is here to help support your child through their anxiety and concerns. Below you'll find guidance and tips from our family to yours.

#### What are anxiety disorders?

Anxiety disorders can cause extreme fear and worry, and change a child's behavior, sleep, eating, or mood.

## Important anxiety topics for families

### Generalized anxiety disorder

*   [Anxiety (for teens)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/teens/anxiety.html?ref=search "Anxiety (for teens)") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Anxiety disorders (for parents)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/anxiety-disorders.html?ref=search "Anxiety disorders") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Anxiety disorders fact sheet (for schools)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/anxiety-factsheet.html?ref=search "Anxiety disorders fact sheet (for schools)") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Stigmas of mental health care in children](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-podcast-critical-role-of-pediatricians-in-the-mental-health-crisis-with-alice-phillips-md/ "Stigmas of mental health care in children") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Critical role of pediatricians in the mental health crisis](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-podcast-stigmas-mental-health-care-in-children-rachel-talbot-md-cook-childrens-hospital/ "Critical role of pediatricians in the mental health crisis") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Quick guide to generalized anxiety disorder](https://childmind.org/guide/quick-guide-to-generalized-anxiety-disorder/ "Quick guide to generalized anxiety disorder") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Quick facts on generalized anxiety disorder](https://childmind.org/article/quick-facts-on-generalized-anxiety-disorder/) | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Generalized anxiety disorder in kids](https://childmind.org/article/generalized-anxiety-disorder-in-kids/ "Generalized anxiety disorder in kids") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Generalized anxiety disorder - self-care](https://medlineplus.gov/ency/patientinstructions/000685.htm "Generalized anxiety disorder - self-care") | _MedlinePlus_
*   [Generalized anxiety disorder: when worry fets out of control](https://www.nimh.nih.gov/health/publications/generalized-anxiety-disorder-gad "Generalized anxiety disorder: when worry fets out of control") | _National Institute of Mental Health_
*   [Anxiety and children](https://www.aacap.org/AACAP/Families_and_Youth/Facts_for_Families/FFF-Guide/The-Anxious-Child-047.aspx "Anxiety and children") | _The American Academy of Child and Adolescent Psychiatry_

### Panic disorder with panic attacks

*   [Panic disorder](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-panic-disorder.html?ref=search "Panic disorder") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Panic disorder factsheet (for schools)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/panic-factsheet.html?ref=search "Panic disorder factsheet (for schools) ") | _Cook Children's_

### Recommended books that address anxiety

*   [Anxious Kids, Anxious Parents: 7 Ways to Stop the Worry Cycle and Raise Courageous and Independent Children](https://a.co/d/dz8STcv "Anxious Kids, Anxious Parents: 7 Ways to Stop the Worry Cycle and Raise Courageous and Independent Children (Anxiety Series)")by Reid Wilson & Lynn Lyons
*   [Bloom: 50 Things to Say, Think, and Do with Anxious, Angry, and Over-the-Top Kids](https://a.co/d/6GkpRId "Bloom: 50 Things to Say, Think, and Do with Anxious, Angry, and Over-the-Top Kids") by Lynne Kenny & Wendy Young
*   [Freeing your Child from Anxiety, Revised and Updated Edition: Practical Strategies to Overcome Fears, Worries, and Phobias and Be Prepared for Life – from Toddlers to Teens](https://a.co/d/ha8aq8Z "Freeing your Child from Anxiety, Revised and Updated Edition: Practical Strategies to Overcome Fears, Worries, and Phobias and Be Prepared for Life – from Toddlers to Teens") by Tamar E. Chanksy
*   [Making Your Worrier a Warrior: A Guide to Conquering Your Child’s Fears](https://a.co/d/ctKnE9I "Making Your Worrier a Warrior: A Guide to Conquering Your Child’s Fears") by Daniel B. Peters
*   [Parenting Your Anxious Child with Mindfulness and Acceptance: A Powerful New Approach to Overcoming Fear, Panic, and Worry Using Acceptance and Commitment Therapy](https://a.co/d/8wMnJ2L "Parenting Your Anxious Child with Mindfulness and Acceptance: A Powerful New Approach to Overcoming Fear, Panic, and Worry Using Acceptance and Commitment Therapy") by Christopher McCurry, PhD
*   [The Anxiety Cure for Kids, Second Edition: A Guide for Parents](http://The Anxiety Cure for Kids, Second Edition  A Guide for Parents "The Anxiety Cure for Kids, Second Edition:  A Guide for Parents") by Elizabeth DuPont Spencer, Robert L. DuPont, and Caroline M. DuPont

## Additional resources for families

## Raising Joy podcast

We encourage you to subscribe to our **Raising Joy podcast**, which aims to encourage hope and resilience among children and teens. Available on the following networks:

[Joy Campaign](https://www.cookchildrens.org/about/promise-report/everything-for-the-child/joy-campaign/ "Joy Campaign")

[Listen on Apple](https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/raising-joy/id1611665146 "Apple podcast")

[Listen on Spotify](https://open.spotify.com/show/6jugpgE9qVbs0xgpFVsxNT "Listen on Spotify")

## Behavioral health services

Our licensed experts provide **psychology and psychiatry services** for families whose children and adolescents, ages 2 to 18, are experiencing behavioral, neurodevelopmental and emotional challenges.

[Behavioral Health department](https://www.cookchildrens.org/services/behavioral-health/ "Behavioral Health")

[Contact us](https://www.cookchildrens.org/services/behavioral-health/contact-us/?postloginurl=inside.asp?mode=patprefs&liteMode=False "Contact us")

Finding health information you can trust can be confusing and overwhelming. Let us help. A Cook Children's librarian can send you up to date information from reliable sources.

# Depression Resources

 In This Section 

*   [Behavior and Emotion Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/)

*   [ADHD Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/adhd/)
*   [Anxiety Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/anxiety/)
*   [Behavior Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/behavior/)
*   [Depression Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/depression/)
*   [Self-Injury/Suicide Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/self-injury-suicide/)
*   [Substance Abuse Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/substance-abuse/)

[![Image 13: Raising Joy Podcast](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/health-resources/mental-health/promo-raisingjoy2.png)](https://www.cookchildrens.org/Recycle-Bin/raising-joy/ "Raising Joy podcast")

![Image 14: Language toggle English](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/interface/language_toggle_eng.png)

It's normal to feel sad, act grouchy, or be in a bad mood at times. But when a sad or bad mood lasts for weeks or longer, and when there are other changes in behavior, it might be depression.

![Image 15: Signs you might be dealing with depression](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/resources/mental-health/info-depression.png)

## Important depression topics for families

Cook Children's offers these depression resources for families. They will help you learn how to provide comfort to your loved one.

### Overview of major depressive disorder

*   [Childhood depression: What parents need to know](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/understanding-depression.html?ref=search "Childhood depression: What parents need to know")| _Cook Children's_
*   [Depression: What you need to know (for teens)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/teens/depression.html?ref=search "Depression: What you need to know (for teens)")| _Cook Children's_
*   [Critical role of pediatricians in the mental health crisis](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-podcast-critical-role-of-pediatricians-in-the-mental-health-crisis-with-alice-phillips-md/ "Critical role of pediatricians in the mental health crisis") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Stigmas of mental health care in children](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-podcast-stigmas-mental-health-care-in-children-rachel-talbot-md-cook-childrens-hospital/ "Stigmas of mental health care in children") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Quick facts on depression](https://childmind.org/article/quick-facts-on-depression/ "Quick facts on depression") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Quick guide to depression in kids](https://childmind.org/guide/depression-in-kids-quick-guide/ "Quick guide to depression in kids") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [What are the kinds of depression](https://childmind.org/article/what-are-the-kinds-of-depression/ "What are the kinds of depression") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Depression](https://www.nimh.nih.gov/health/topics/depression "Depression") | _National Institute of Mental Health_

### Bipolar disorder signs and symptoms

*   [Bipolar disorder (for teens)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/teens/bipolar.html?ref=search "Bipolar disorder (for teens)") | _Cook Children's_
*   [What should I do if I think I have bipolar disorder? (for teens)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/teens/bipolar-tips.html?ref=search "What should I do if I think I have bipolar disorder? (for teens)") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Bipolar disorder factsheet (for schools)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/bipolar-factsheet.html?ref=search "Bipolar disorder factsheet (for schools)") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Quick guide to bipolar disorder in kids](https://childmind.org/guide/bipolar-disorder-in-kids-quick-guide/ "Quick guide to bipolar disorder in kids") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Quick facts on bipolar disorder](https://childmind.org/article/quick-facts-on-bipolar-disorder/ "Quick facts on bipolar disorder") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [The depressed child](https://www.aacap.org/AACAP/Families_and_Youth/Facts_for_Families/FFF-Guide/The-Depressed-Child-004.aspx "The depressed child") | _The American Academy of Child and Adolescent Psychiatry_
*   [Bi-polar disorder](https://www.nimh.nih.gov/health/topics/bipolar-disorder "Bi-polar disorder") | _National Institute of Mental Health_

### Information about medications for depression

*   [Medication for kids with depression](https://childmind.org/article/medication-for-kids-with-depression/ "Medications for kids with depression") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [What medications are most effective in children with bipolar disorder](https://childmind.org/article/what-medications-are-most-effective-in-children-with-bipolar-disorder/ "What medications are most effective in children with bipolar disorder") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Mental health medications](https://www.nimh.nih.gov/health/topics/mental-health-medications "Mental health medications") | _National Institute of Mental Health_

### Maternal depression

This video from Cook Children's covers the signs, facts and resources available for maternal depression.

*   Describes the connection between mental health, oral health and overall health.
*   How to recognize depression and the role dental and medical providers play.
*   Assess maternal mental health.
*   Identify where to go for resources.

Maternal Depression | Ask the Docs | Cook Children's![Image 16](https://img.youtube.com/vi/TZIczqjVrxE/hqdefault.jpg)

*   [Encouraging good sleep habits](https://childmind.org/article/encouraging-good-sleep-habits/ "Encouraging good sleep habits") | _Child Mind Institute_

## Behavioral health services

[![Image 11: Raising Joy Podcast](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/health-resources/mental-health/promo-raisingjoy2.png)](https://www.cookchildrens.org/Recycle-Bin/raising-joy/ "Raising Joy podcast")

![Image 12: Language toggle English](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/interface/language_toggle_eng.png)

Behavior tips and resources selected by Cook Children's staff for your family. These will help guide your child with patience and care.

#### What is behavioral health?

Behavioral health is medical care that helps manage emotions and behavior. Doctors who work in behavioral health are psychologists and psychiatrists.

## Important behavior topics for families

### Disruptive Mood Dysregulation Disorder (DMDD)

*   [Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder and ADHD](https://www.additudemag.com/disruptive-mood-dysregulation-disorder-and-adhd/ "Disruptive mood disorder and ADHD") | _ADDitude Magazine_
*   [Quick facts on disruptive mood dysregulation disorder (DMDD)](https://childmind.org/article/quick-facts-on-disruptive-mood-dysregulation-disorder-dmdd/ "Quick facts on DMDD") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Quick guide for disruptive modd dysregulation disorder](https://childmind.org/guide/disruptive-mood-dysregulation-disorder-a-quick-guide/ "Quick guide to DMDD") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder](https://www.nimh.nih.gov/health/topics/disruptive-mood-dysregulation-disorder-dmdd/disruptive-mood-dysregulation-disorder "Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder") | _National Institute of Mental Health_
*   [Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder](https://www.aacap.org/AACAP/Families_and_Youth/Facts_for_Families/FFF-Guide/Disruptive-Mood-Dysregulation-Disorder-_DMDD_-110.aspx "Disruptive mood dysregulation disorder") | _The American Academy of Child and Adolescent Psychiatry_

### Recommended books on behavior

*   [Help! There’s a Toddler in the House!](https://a.co/d/6bR1GrS "Help! There’s a Toddler in the House!") by Thomas M. Reimers, Ph.D. (for parents of kids aged 2-6yo)
*   [Common Sense Parenting of Toddlers and Preschoolers](https://www.amazon.com/Common-Sense-Parenting-Toddlers-Preschoolers/dp/1889322415 "Common Sense Parenting of Toddlers and Preschoolers") by Bridget Barnes (for parents of kids aged 2-5yo)
*   [The Kazdin Method for Parenting the Defiant Child](https://www.amazon.com/Kazdin-Method-Parenting-Defiant-Child/dp/0547085826 "The Kazdin Method"). By Alan E. Kazdin. He also has a free online course with video lectures at [https://www.coursera.org/learn/everyday-parenting](https://www.coursera.org/learn/everyday-parenting "The Kazdin Method for Parenting the Defiant Child"). When you enter the course, it states that it takes 21 hours to complete. That is for people who want to earn a course certificate and complete additional readings and quizzes. You can simply enroll and click on the applicable videos that you want to watch.
*   [Your Defiant Child](https://a.co/d/1QEeeZD "Your Defiant Child") by Russell A. Barkley and Christine Benton (for parents of kids aged 5-12)
*   [The Explosive Child](https://a.co/d/1JEZu9M "The Explosive Child") by Ross W. Greene

# Self-Injury/Suicide Resources

 In This Section 

*   [Behavior and Emotion Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/)

*   [ADHD Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/adhd/)
*   [Anxiety Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/anxiety/)
*   [Behavior Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/behavior/)
*   [Depression Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/depression/)
*   [Self-Injury/Suicide Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/self-injury-suicide/)
*   [Substance Abuse Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/substance-abuse/)

[![Image 13: Raising Joy Podcast](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/health-resources/mental-health/promo-raisingjoy2.png)](https://www.cookchildrens.org/Recycle-Bin/raising-joy/ "Raising Joy podcast")

![Image 14: Language toggle English](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/interface/language_toggle_eng.png)

During challenging times, these caring resources have been handpicked to help families like yours, offering guidance and understanding as you support your child through difficult emotions and find healthier ways to cope and heal together.

![Image 15: Call 988 if you have feelings about suicide.](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/resources/mental-health/info-selfharm-988.png)

## Important self-injury/suicide topics for families

### Suicide and self injury statistics

*   [Researching the rise in child suicides](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-podcast-researching-the-mystifying-rise-in-child-suicides-with-suzy-deyoung/ "Researching the rise in child suicides") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Preventing youth suicides](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-podcast-not-one-more-preventing-youth-suicides-with-lynda-clayton/ "Preventing youth suicides") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Conversations matter (man who lost his son to suicide)](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-podcast-conversations-matter-brad-hunstable-haydens-corner-mental-health-cook-childrens/ "Conversations matter (man who lost his son to suicide)") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Three parents open up about losing a child to suicide](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/in-their-own-words-three-parents-open-up-about-losing-a-child-to-suicide/ "In their own words: Three parents open up about losing a child to suicide") | _Cook Children's_

### Warning signs of suicide

*   [I'm thinking of suicide. How can I get help? (for teens)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/teens/stop-suicide.html?WT.ac=ctg) | _Cook Children's_
*   [Preventing suicides: Tom and Ellen Harris lost their daughter to suicide without much warning](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-preventing-suicides-with-tom-and-ellen-harris/ "Preventing suicides: Tom and Ellen Harris lost their daughter to suicide without much warning") | _Cook Children's_
*   [Signs a child might be suicidal](https://childmind.org/article/signs-a-child-might-be-suicidal/ "Signs a child might be suicidal") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Teen suicides: What are the risk factors?](https://childmind.org/article/teen-suicides-risk-factors/ "Teen suicides: What are the risk factors?") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [How ca`n you prevent suicide?](https://www.nimh.nih.gov/health/topics/suicide-prevention "How can you prevent suicide?") | _The National Institute of Mental Health (NIMH)_
*   [Warning signs of suicide](https://www.nimh.nih.gov/health/publications/warning-signs-of-suicide "Warning signs of suicide") | _The National Institute of Mental Health (NIMH)_

### Why kids self injure

*   [I started cutting again. How can I stop? (for teens)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/teens/cutting-relapse.html?WT.ac=ctg)| _Cook Children's_
*   [Cutting and self-injury (for teens)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/teens/cutting.html?ref=search "Cutting and self-injury (for teens)")| _Cook Children's_
*   [Cutting and self-harm factsheet (for schools)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/cutting-factsheet.html?ref=search "Cutting and self-harm factsheet (for schools)")| _Cook Children's_
*   [Helping teens who self-harm](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/help-cutting.html?ref=search "Helping teens who self-harm")_| Cook Children's_
*   [Quick facts on self-injury](https://childmind.org/article/quick-facts-on-self-injury/ "Quick facts on self-injury") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Help for cutting and other self-injury](https://childmind.org/article/what-drives-self-injury-and-how-to-treat-it/ "Help for cutting and other self-injury") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Why do young people hurt themselves?](https://childmind.org/article/why-do-young-people-hurt-themselves/ "Why do young people hurt themselves?") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Self-injury in adolescents](https://www.aacap.org/AACAP/Families_and_Youth/Facts_for_Families/FFF-Guide/Self-Injury-In-Adolescents-073.aspx "Self-injury in adolescents") | _The American Academy of Child and Adolescent Psychiatry_

### When does self injury lead to suicide

*   [Suicide in children and teens](https://www.aacap.org/AACAP/Families_and_Youth/Facts_for_Families/FFF-Guide/Teen-Suicide-010.aspx "Suicide in children and teens") | _The American Academy of Child and Adolescent Psychiatry_

### Safety tips

*   [What to do if you're worried about suicide](https://childmind.org/article/youre-worried-suicide/ "What to do if you're worried about suicide") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Gun safety with Dr. Guzman](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-podcast-gun-safety-with-daniel-guzman-md/ "Gun safety with Dr. Guzman") | _Cook Children's_

### Safety plan guide

*   [Reducing suicide risk with safety plans](https://childmind.org/article/what-is-a-safety-plan/ "Reducing suicide risk with safety plans") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Safety plan guide to fill out for families](https://www.mysafetyplan.org/static/NationalSPA-c4a86b10761e54a2dd835519b48ff479.pdf "Safety plan guide to fill out for families to fill out")| _Vibrant Emotional health_

### Different levels of care

*   [Taking a child to the emergency room](https://childmind.org/article/taking-a-child-to-the-emergency-room/ "Taking a child to the emergency room") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Having a child in emergency inpatient treatment](https://childmind.org/article/having-child-inpatient-treatment-psychiatric-hospital/ "Having a child in emergency inpatient treatment") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Bringing a child home from psychiatric hospitalization](https://childmind.org/article/bringing-child-home-psychiatric-hospitalization/ "Bringing a child home from psychiatric hospitalization") | _Child Mind Institute_
*   [Improving the medical response to kids with a mental health crisis](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-podcast-improving-the-medical-response-to-kids-experiencing-a-mental-health-crisis/ "Improving the medical response to kids with a mental health crisis") | _Cook Children's_
*   [When does a child need inpatient psychiatric care with Dr. Kia Carter](https://www.checkupnewsroom.com/raising-joy-podcast-when-a-child-needs-inpatient-psychiatric-care-with-kia-carter-md/ "When does a child need inpatient psychiatric care with Dr. Kia Carter") | _Cook Children's_

## Need help finding information?

Finding health information you can trust can be confusing and overwhelming. Let us help. A Cook Children's librarian can send you up to date information from reliable sources.

## Behavioral health services

Our licensed experts provide **psychology and psychiatry services** for families whose children and adolescents, ages 2 to 18, are experiencing behavioral, neurodevelopmental and emotional challenges.

[![Image 17](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/checkup-resources/doc-right-rail-banner-like-family.png)](https://www.cookchildrens.org/visit/pediatrician-offices/)

![Image 18: Language toggle English](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/interface/language_toggle_eng.png)

Your child's health and wellness play a vital role in nurturing their well-being. Health and wellness for kids encompass so much more than just physical health. It's about their overall well-being - their physical, mental, and emotional health all rolled into one. Here, you'll discover fun ways to promote healthy habits, nurture growing minds and bodies, and create a home filled with love and well-being. By building a healthy foundation, you're empowering them for a lifetime of wellbeing.

![Image 19](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/checkup-resources/cc_icon_healthwellness_emotionalwellbeing.svg)

## Building a strong foundation together

Discover the many ways family life impacts how kids learn, gain self-esteem and grow up to become healthy adults.

Select an option...

Select an option...

Healthy families

# Family Life Resources

 In This Section 

*   [Checkup Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/)

*   [Behavior and Emotion Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/mental-health/)
*   [Conditions and Diagnoses](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/conditions/)
*   [Family Life Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/family-life/)
    *   [Family Fun and Activities](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/family-life/family-fun-and-activities/)
    *   [Guidance and Discipline Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/family-life/discipline/)
    *   [Healthy Families Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/family-life/healthy-families/)
    *   [Healthy Home Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/family-life/healthy-home/)

    *   [Safe Travel Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/family-life/safe-travel-resources/)

*   [Fitness and Nutrition Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/fitness-and-nutrition/)
*   [Growth and Development Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/growth-and-development/)
*   [Health and Wellness](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/health-and-wellness/)
*   [Immunization and Vaccine Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/immunizations-and-vaccines/)
*   [Know Where to Go](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/know-where-to-go/)
*   [Medication Information](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/medication-information/)
*   [Prenatal and Newborn Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/newborn/)
*   [Safety and Injury Prevention Resources](https://www.cookchildrens.org/health-resources/safety-and-injury-prevention/)

[![Image 18](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/checkup-resources/doc-right-rail-banner-like-family.png)](https://www.cookchildrens.org/visit/pediatrician-offices/)

![Image 19: Language toggle English](https://www.cookchildrens.org/siteassets/images/interface/language_toggle_eng.png)

Family is super important to a child's wellbeing. It's where we learn, grow, and have lots of fun – together. Family also plays a big role in how kids grow up to be healthy adults. The way we eat, exercise and take care of each other at home can make a big difference in how strong and happy we feel physically, mentally and emotionally. When families support each other, talk about feelings and do things like playing together or eating healthy meals, it helps everyone stay fit and feel good. We invite you to explore healthy ways your family can feel awesome together!

## 8. A to Z: Atrial Septal Defect (ASD) (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-asd.html

Title: A to Z: Atrial Septal Defect (ASD) (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-asd.html

Markdown Content:
**May also be called: ASD**

An atrial septal defect, or [ASD](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/asd.html) — sometimes referred to as a hole in the [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html) — is a type of [congenital heart defect](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-asd.html) in which there is an abnormal opening in the dividing wall between the upper filling chambers of the heart (the atria).

### More to Know

The heart has four chambers: The two lower pumping chambers (the ventricles) and the two upper filling chambers (the atria). [Blood](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/blood.html) that is low in oxygen returns from the body to the right atrium before passing to the right ventricle and then to the lungs to receive oxygen. Oxygen-rich blood returns to the left atrium before passing to the left ventricle, where it is pumped out to the rest of the body.

The right and left atria are separated by a thin shared wall called the atrial septum. Kids with an ASD are born with an opening in this wall that allows oxygen-rich and oxygen-poor blood to mix, increasing the total amount of blood that flows toward the lungs. The blood flowing through the hole creates an extra noise, known as a heart murmur, that can be heard when a doctor listens to the heart with a stethoscope.

Treatment for an ASD depends on the child's age and the size, location, and severity of the defect. Very small ASDs may close on their own. Larger ASDs usually won't close and must be treated medically. Most of these can be closed in a [cardiac catheterization](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/cardiac-catheter.html) lab, although some will require open-heart surgery. Large ASDs can cause symptoms like poor appetite, poor growth, fatigue, shortness of breath, and lung problems or infections, such as [pneumonia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/pneumonia.html).

### Keep in Mind

A small ASD will usually close without treatment within the first 2 years of a child's life. If a larger ASD is not treated, health complications can develop later, but most kids with ASDs are diagnosed and treated long before the heart defect causes physical symptoms. Typically, after repair and adequate time for healing, kids with ASDs rarely have further symptoms.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._

---

## 9. A to Z: Atrioventricular Septal Defect (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atrioventricular.html

Title: A to Z: Atrioventricular Septal Defect (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atrioventricular.html

Markdown Content:
**May also be called: Endocardial Cushion Defect; ECD; Atrioventricular Canal Defect**

An atrioventricular septal defect is an abnormal heart condition caused by a poorly formed central area of the [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html). Atrioventricular septal defects are [congenital](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atrioventricular.html), meaning they are present at birth.

### More to Know

The heart consists of four chambers — the left atrium and left ventricle, and the right atrium and right ventricle. The chambers are separated by a wall of tissue called the septum. Two valves — the mitral and tricuspid valves — separate the atria (plural of atrium) from the ventricles.

With atrioventricular septal defects, the tissues that form the septum don't grow completely while a baby is in the womb, leaving one or more holes between the atria or the ventricles. In some cases, instead of two separate valves, there is only one large common valve, which may be malformed (formed incorrectly).

The causes of atrioventricular septal defects aren't fully understood, but they're commonly seen in children with [Down syndrome](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/down-syndrome.html). The defects can make the heart have to work harder to pump blood and cause symptoms like difficulty feeding, failure to gain weight, lung congestion, and a bluish tint to the skin (called cyanosis).

Atrioventricular septal defects are usually corrected through surgery while a child is still an infant.

### Keep in Mind

If left untreated, an atrioventricular septal defect can cause complications (including heart failure) and may be life threatening. Once surgery has been done to correct the defect, however, most kids lead a normal life.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._

---

## 10. A to Z: Atresia, Aortic (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-aortic.html

Title: A to Z: Atresia, Aortic (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-aortic.html

Markdown Content:
Atresia (ah-TREE-zhah) is a condition in which a baby is born with a missing or closed valve or tube somewhere in his or her body. Aortic atresia is a rare defect that involves valves in the [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html).

### More to Know

Air, [blood](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/blood.html), bodily fluids, and waste products travel throughout the body in a system of vessels, tubes, and chambers that are often separated by valves. When a child is born with atresia, it means that a valve is missing or a tube is closed off. This interrupts the normal flow of blood, fluid, waste, or air, which can lead to a number of complications.

Most kinds of atresia are serious and can be fatal if they go untreated. Treatment usually involves [surgery](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-aortic.html) while the child is still an infant.

Atresia can affect many body parts, including the nose, ears, organs, [digestive](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/digestive.html) tract, and heart. The types of atresia are named for the body parts they affect:

*   [Tricuspid atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-tricuspid.html) and[pulmonary atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-pulmonary.html) also involve valves in the heart.
*   [Choanal atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-choanal.html) is a defect of the nasal passages (choana).
*   [Biliary atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-biliary.html) is a defect in the liver or bile system.
*   [Anal atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-anal.html) (imperforate anus) and [esophageal atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-esophageal.html) are defects of the digestive tract.

### Keep in Mind

Most kinds of atresia can be treated successfully with surgery; some cases may require more than one operation.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._

---

## 11. A to Z: Atresia, Pulmonary (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-pulmonary.html

Title: A to Z: Atresia, Pulmonary (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-pulmonary.html

Markdown Content:
Atresia (ah-TREE-zhah) is a condition in which a baby is born with a missing or closed valve or tube somewhere in his or her body.

Pulmonary atresia is a rare defect in which a baby is born with an abnormally developed pulmonary [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html) valve (which is between two of the heart's chambers) that doesn't open. This prevents blood from flowing through the heart and into the lungs to receive oxygen. Treatments include medications and surgery.

### More to Know

Air, [blood](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/blood.html), bodily fluids, and waste products travel throughout the body in a system of vessels, tubes, and chambers that are often separated by valves. When a child is born with atresia, it means that a valve is missing or a tube is closed off. This interrupts the normal flow of blood, fluid, waste, or air, which can lead to a number of complications.

Most kinds of atresia are serious and can be fatal if they go untreated. Treatment usually involves [surgery](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-pulmonary.html) while the child is still an infant.

Atresia can affect many body parts, including the nose, ears, organs, digestive tract, and heart. The types of atresia are named for the body parts they affect:

*   [Tricuspid atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-tricuspid.html) and [aortic atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-aortic.html) also involve valves in the heart.
*   [Biliary atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-biliary.html) is a defect in the liver or bile system.
*   [Choanal atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-choanal.html) is a defect of the nasal passages (choana).
*   [Anal atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-anal.html) (imperforate anus) and [esophageal atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-esophageal.html) are defects of the digestive tract.

### Keep in Mind

Most kinds of atresia can be treated successfully with surgery; some cases may require more than one operation.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._

## 12. A to Z: Atresia, Tricuspid (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-tricuspid.html

Title: A to Z: Atresia, Tricuspid (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-tricuspid.html

Markdown Content:
Atresia (ah-TREE-zhah) is a condition in which a baby is born with a missing or closed valve or tube somewhere in his or her body.

Tricuspid atresia is a rare defect in which a baby is born with an abnormally developed tricuspid [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html) valve (which is between two of the heart's chambers). This prevents blood from flowing through the heart and into the lungs to receive oxygen. It is treated surgically.

### More to Know

Air, [blood](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/blood.html), bodily fluids, and waste products travel throughout the body in a system of vessels, tubes, and chambers that are often separated by valves. When a child is born with atresia, it means that a valve is missing or a tube is closed off. This interrupts the normal flow of blood, fluid, waste, or air, which can lead to a number of complications.

Most kinds of atresia are serious and can be fatal if they go untreated. Treatment usually involves surgery while the child is still an infant.

Atresia can affect many body parts, including the nose, ears, organs, [digestive](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/digestive.html) tract, and heart. The types of atresia are named for the body parts they affect:

*   [Pulmonary atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-pulmonary.html) and [aortic atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-aortic.html) also involve valves in the heart.
*   [Choanal atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-choanal.html) is a defect of the nasal passages (choana).
*   [Biliary atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-biliary.html) is a defect in the liver or bile system.
*   [Anal atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-anal.html) (imperforate anus) and [esophageal atresia](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-atresia-esophageal.html) are defects of the digestive tract.

### Keep in Mind

Most kinds of atresia can be treated successfully with surgery; some cases may require more than one operation.

## 13. A to Z: Aortic Stenosis (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-aortic-stenosis.html

Title: A to Z: Aortic Stenosis (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-aortic-stenosis.html

Markdown Content:
[![Image 1: A to Z Dictionary 500 Go](https://kidshealth.org/content/dam/kidshealth/en/buttons/P-atoZDictionary-enBT.jpg)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/dictionary/)

**May also be called: Aortic Valve Stenosis**

The aortic valve is one of two valves that control the flow of blood as it leaves the [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html). (The other is the pulmonary valve.) These valves work to keep the blood flowing forward. They open up to let the blood move ahead, then close quickly to keep the blood from flowing backward.

In aortic stenosis (ay-OR-tik stuh-NO-sis),the aortic valve is too narrow and can't open all the way.

### More to Know

The aorta, the body's largest blood vessel, starts from the left ventricle of the heart and carries oxygen-rich blood to the body. Blood flows from the left ventricle into the aorta through the aortic valve, one of the four valves in the heart.

In aortic stenosis, the aortic valve is narrow. This decreases the amount of blood flowing into the aorta and out to the rest of the body. Aortic stenosis is most common in adults over 50, but can be present at birth ([congenital](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-aortic-stenosis.html)).

Aortic stenosis makes the heart work harder to pump blood to the body. Over time, this added stress can weaken the heart and lead to life-threatening heart problems.

Aortic stenosis can be identified before birth, allowing babies born with severe cases to be treated right away. Babies with aortic stenosis can have trouble gaining weight, problems with feeding, and serious breathing problems that develop soon after birth. Older children also may have a [heart murmur](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/murmurs.html). These children may be sent for an echocardiogram, a type of heart ultrasound that will show how the valves are working.

People with severe aortic stenosis may have chest pain and shortness of breath, feel tired or dizzy, and have abnormal heartbeats. Mild cases of aortic stenosis may not need treatment. Medicines sometimes can treat the symptoms of aortic stenosis, but it can only be corrected through surgery.

### Keep in Mind

Many people with aortic stenosis have no symptoms. Others have mild symptoms that never become a problem. In severe cases, however, the valve needs to be surgically repaired or replaced. Aortic stenosis often can be treated without open-heart surgery through a less invasive procedure called a [cardiac catheterization](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/cardiac-catheter.html). In young children with a severe problem, this usually involves a procedure called balloon valvuloplasty, in which an unopened balloon is threaded through the aortic valve and inflated to open the valve.

Kids and teens with moderate or severe aortic stenosis should avoid sports. Physical activity can increase blood flow, which can put added stress on the heart and lead to a medical emergency.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._

---

## 14. A to Z: Coarctation of the Aorta (COA) (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-coa.html

Title: A to Z: Coarctation of the Aorta (COA) (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-coa.html

Markdown Content:
[![Image 1: A to Z Dictionary 500 Go](https://kidshealth.org/content/dam/kidshealth/en/buttons/P-atoZDictionary-enBT.jpg)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/dictionary/)

The aorta is the major artery that carries blood away from the [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html) to the body. When someone has [coarctation](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/coa.html) (ko-ark-TAY-shun) of the aorta (COA), it means the aorta is narrowed at some point.

### More to Know

When part of the aorta is narrowed, the defect (coarctation) can affect the body's blood circulation because the left side of the heart has to work harder to pump blood through the narrowed aorta. Sometimes the narrowing is minor and might not even cause symptoms. In other cases, the aorta may be more constricted, placing a strain on the heart's left ventricle (the chamber that pumps blood to the aorta and out to the body).

A coarctation can occur anywhere in the aorta, but most often is found just beyond the point where the arteries that carry blood to the upper body and head branch off from the aorta.

### Keep in Mind

Doctors often recommend that COA be treated quickly, especially in teens and adults. The longer a COA is left untreated, the more likely it is that the person will have high blood pressure even after the COA is fixed. If it's left untreated indefinitely, the defect can be fatal in many people by the age of 40.

Surgery and other procedures are used to treat COAs. These include removing the narrow section and reconnecting the two good ends of the aorta, or using a procedure (called balloon dilation or balloon angioplasty) to expand the narrow area.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._

---

## 15. A to Z: Complete Transposition of the Great Vessels (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-complete-transposition.html

Title: A to Z: Complete Transposition of the Great Vessels (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-complete-transposition.html

Markdown Content:
_May also be called: Complete Transposition of the Great Arteries; Transposition of the Great Vessels; Transposition of the Great Arteries_

Complete transposition (trans-puh-ZIH-shun) of the great vessels is a [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html) defect where the aorta and the pulmonary artery (called the "great vessels" or "great arteries") are reversed, causing the heart to work incorrectly and preventing blood from getting oxygen.

### More to Know

The human heart has four chambers: the right atrium, left atrium, right ventricle, and left ventricle. In a healthy heart, oxygen-poor blood from the body enters the heart through the right atrium. Blood then flows to the right ventricle and is pumped to the lungs through the pulmonary artery to pick up oxygen. The oxygen-rich blood then comes back to the heart through the left atrium. The blood flows to the left ventricle and takes the oxygen to the body through the aorta.

When someone has a complete transposition of the great vessels, the pulmonary artery and the aorta are switched so that the aorta is on the right side of the heart and receives oxygen-poor blood, which is sent right back out to the body without getting more oxygen. The pulmonary artery is on the left side of the heart, receives oxygen-rich blood, and sends it back to the lungs again. So, oxygen-rich blood cannot get to the body.

Babies with complete transpositions of the great vessels often appear very blue and have low oxygen levels in the bloodstream. They may have trouble feeding and problems breathing. Without treatment, transposition can be life threatening.

### Keep in Mind

Treatment for complete transposition of the great vessels usually involves a surgical procedure called an arterial switch, where the aorta is attached to the left ventricle and the pulmonary artery is attached to the right ventricle. Although those who have had complete transposition of the great vessels need lifelong follow-up with a cardiologist, arterial switch allows most to go on to lead normal, healthy lives.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._

---

## 16. A to Z: Ebstein's Anomaly (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-ebstein.html

Title: A to Z: Ebstein's Anomaly (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-ebstein.html

Markdown Content:
Ebstein's anomaly is a rare congenital (present at birth) [defect](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/if-heart-defect.html) in the right side of the [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html). The cause is unknown.

## More to Know

Someone with Ebstein's anomaly has a malformed (not formed correctly) and improperly positioned tricuspid valve. The tricuspid valve separates the two chambers on the right side of the heart. In a person with Ebstein's anomaly, the valve doesn't close properly, which causes blood to leak back from the lower chamber (ventricle) to the upper chamber (atrium). This disrupts [blood](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/blood.html) flow and makes the heart work inefficiently, which can lead to enlargement of the right atrium, insufficient red blood supply to the body, or heart failure.

Ebstein's anomaly varies in severity from person to person. A newborn showing signs of the condition may be seriously ill and need surgery while someone whose symptoms don't appear until adulthood may not need any treatment.

Signs and symptoms of Ebstein's anomaly include shortness of breath, fatigue, rapid breathing, failure to grow, swelling in the legs, and a bluish skin color around the lips and nails. The condition is often associated with other heart defects, such as [atrial septal defect (ASD)](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/asd.html), pulmonary (valve) stenosis, and abnormal heart rhythms ([arrhythmias](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/arrhythmias.html)).

### Keep in Mind

The long-term outlook for people with Ebstein's anomaly varies greatly, but with treatment and close monitoring by a cardiologist, most people with the disorder can go on to live healthy and productive lives.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._

---

## 17. A to Z: Endocardial Cushion Defect (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-endocardial.html

Title: A to Z: Endocardial Cushion Defect (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-endocardial.html

Markdown Content:
_May also be called: ECD; Atrioventricular Canal Defect; Atrioventricular Septal Defect_

An endocardial (en-doh-CAR-dee-ul) cushion defect is an abnormal heart condition caused by a poorly formed central area of the [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html). Endocardial cushion defects are [congenital](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-endocardial.html), meaning they are present at birth.

### More to Know

The heart consists of four chambers — the left atrium and left ventricle, and the right atrium and right ventricle. The chambers are separated by a wall of tissue called the septum. Two valves — the mitral and tricuspid valves — separate the atria (plural of atrium) from the ventricles.

With endocardial cushion defects, the tissues that form the septum don't grow completely while a baby is in the womb, leaving one or more holes between the atria or the ventricles. In some cases, instead of two separate valves, there is only one large common valve, which may be malformed (formed incorrectly).

The causes of endocardial cushion defects aren't fully understood, but they're commonly seen in children with [Down syndrome](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/down-syndrome.html). The defects can make the heart have to work harder to pump blood and cause symptoms like difficulty feeding, failure to gain weight, lung congestion, and a bluish tint to the skin (called cyanosis).

Endocardial cushion defects are usually corrected through surgery while a child is still an infant.

### Keep in Mind

If left untreated, an endocardial heart defect can cause complications (including heart failure) and may be life threatening. Once surgery has been done to correct the defect, however, most kids lead a normal life.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._

Medically reviewed by: KidsHealth Medical Experts

---

## 18. A to Z: Hypoplastic Left Heart Syndrome (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-hypoplastic.html

Title: A to Z: Hypoplastic Left Heart Syndrome (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-hypoplastic.html

Markdown Content:
_May also be called: HLHS_

Hypoplastic (HI-puh-plas-tik) left heart syndrome (HLHS) is a rare and serious defect in which the structures of the left side of the [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html) (the left ventricle, the mitral valve, and the aortic valve) are underdeveloped. As a result, [blood](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/blood.html) cannot be adequately pumped throughout the body.

### More to Know

Hypoplastic left heart syndrome is present at birth ([congenital](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-hypoplastic.html)) and has no known cause. It is usually diagnosed within the first few days of life. Without surgery to repair the heart, HLHS is fatal.

Symptoms of HLHS include blue or gray skin color (cyanosis), rapid breathing, pounding heart, shortness of breath, cold hands and feet, weak pulse, unusual drowsiness and poor feeding.

Once diagnosed with HLHS, most babies will undergo a series of three operations beginning shortly after birth and ending at 3 years of age. For some babies, [heart transplant](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart-transplant.html) is the best option if a donated organ is available.

### Keep in Mind

While many babies now survive HLHS, they need to be monitored closely by a cardiologist for the rest of their lives. Many complications can occur with HLHS and sometimes additional heart surgery or even heart transplant may be necessary as children born with HLHS get older.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._

## 19. A to Z: Interrupted Aortic Arch (for Parents)

**Source:** https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-interrupted-aortic-arch.html

Title: A to Z: Interrupted Aortic Arch (for Parents)

URL Source: https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-interrupted-aortic-arch.html

Markdown Content:
**May also be called: IAA; Aortic Arch Interruption**

Interrupted aortic (ay-OR-tik) arch is a rare congenital (present at [birth](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/az-interrupted-aortic-arch.html)) problem. It happens when a baby's aorta doesn't develop correctly, leaving a gap between two parts of the aorta that are normally connected.

### More to Know

The aorta, the body's largest blood vessel, carries oxygen-rich blood from the [heart](https://kidshealth.org/CookChildrens/en/parents/heart.html) to the rest of the body. It starts from the heart's left ventricle, goes up, and then does a U-turn around the top of the heart before heading down to the rest of the body. The curved part above the heart is the aortic arch.

When an aortic arch is interrupted it means that at some point along the curve, the part going up (the ascending aorta) ends and is not attached to the part going down (the descending aorta). This means that the heart can't send blood through the aorta to the lower body.

Interrupted aortic arch (IAA) is a life-threatening condition. When a baby is born with IAA, the only way for the lower body to get blood is through a small blood vessel called the ductus arteriosus. This duct allows most of the blood to bypass the lungs in a developing fetus. It is present when a child is born but usually closes on its own after a day or two. Once the duct closes, a child with IAA needs surgery to fix the interruption and connect the ascending aorta to the descending aorta. Babies with IAA are given medicine to keep the ductus arteriosus open until surgery can be done.

Babies with IAA usually seem healthy at birth but become very ill within the first days of life. Symptoms include rapid breathing, rapid heartbeat, poor feeding, and a gray skin tone in areas that aren't getting any blood.

### Keep in Mind

Doctors can diagnose IAA with an imaging scan while a fetus is still in the womb or after birth with an echocardiogram. After surgery, children treated for IAA usually will take antibiotics for the rest of their lives to prevent heart infections, but their long-term outlook is excellent.

_All A to Z dictionary entries are regularly reviewed by KidsHealth medical experts._
